href="#cite_note-kihon151208-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Smart_Lander_for_Investigating_Moon" title="Smart Lander for Investigating Moon">SLIM</a>, pinpoint <a href="/wiki/Moon_landing" title="Moon landing">lunar lander</a> (LV: Epsilon)</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="FY_2020">FY 2020</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=JAXA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: FY 2020">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li>Advanced Radar Satellite<sup id="cite_ref-kihon151208_34-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kihon151208-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_missions">Other missions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=JAXA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Other missions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>For the 2018 <a href="/wiki/ESA" class="mw-redirect" title="ESA">ESA</a> <a href="/wiki/EarthCARE" title="EarthCARE">EarthCARE</a> mission, JAXA will provide the radar system on the satellite.  JAXA is also providing the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Light_Particle_Telescope&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Light Particle Telescope (page does not exist)">Light Particle Telescope</a> (LPT) for the 2008 <a href="/wiki/Jason_2" class="mw-redirect" title="Jason 2">Jason 2</a> satellite by the French <a href="/wiki/CNES" title="CNES">CNES</a>. JAXA will provide the Auroral Electron Sensor (AES) for the Taiwanese FORMOSAT-5.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/w/index.php?title=SmartSat-1&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="SmartSat-1 (page does not exist)">SmartSat-1</a>, small communication test and sun corona observation, Mission status unclear</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/XEUS" title="XEUS">XEUS</a> joint X-Ray telescope with ESA, launch after 2015.</li>\n<li>Sohla-2 Small PETSAT Demonstration Satellite</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_orientation_of_JAXA">New orientation of JAXA</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=JAXA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: New orientation of JAXA">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Planning interplanetary research missions can take up to seven years, such as the <a href="/wiki/ASTRO-E" class="mw-redirect" title="ASTRO-E">ASTRO-E</a>. Due to the lag time between these interplanetary events and mission planning time, opportunities to gain new knowledge about the cosmos might  be lost. To prevent this, JAXA plans on using smaller, faster missions from 2010 onwards. JAXA is developing a new solid-fueled rocket, the <a href="/wiki/Epsilon_(rocket)" title="Epsilon (rocket)">Epsilon</a>, to replace the retired <a href="/wiki/M-V" title="M-V">M-V</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Developing_projects">Developing projects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=JAXA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Developing projects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/IKAROS" title="IKAROS">IKAROS</a> (Interplanetary Kite-craft Accelerated by Radiation Of the Sun), a small size powered-<a href="/wiki/Solar_sail" title="Solar sail">solar sail</a> experimental spacecraft.  Future mission will use solar sail for <a href="/wiki/Jupiter" title="Jupiter">Jupiter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trojan_asteroid" class="mw-redirect" title="Trojan asteroid">Trojan asteroids</a> exploration.</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Plans">Plans</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=JAXA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Plans">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li>Human Lunar Systems, conceptual system study on the future human lunar outpost</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Nano-JASMINE" title="Nano-JASMINE">Nano-JASMINE</a> - <a href="/w/index.php?title=Small-JASMINE&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Small-JASMINE (page does not exist)">Small-JASMINE</a> - <a href="/w/index.php?title=JASMINE_telescope&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="JASMINE telescope (page does not exist)">JASMINE</a>, a series of astrometric telescopes similar to the <a href="/wiki/Gaia_(spacecraft)" title="Gaia (spacecraft)">Gaia</a> mission but operating in the infra-red (2.2&#160;\xc2\xb5m) and specifically targeting the Galactic plane and centre, where Gaia\'s results are impaired by dust absorption.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Martian_Moons_Explorer" class="mw-redirect" title="Martian Moons Explorer">MMX</a>, remote sensing of <a href="/wiki/Deimos_(moon)" title="Deimos (moon)">Deimos</a>, sample return from <a href="/wiki/Phobos_(moon)" title="Phobos (moon)">Phobos</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/LiteBIRD" title="LiteBIRD">LiteBIRD</a>, a mission to study <a href="/wiki/Cosmic_microwave_background#Polarization" title="Cosmic microwave background">CMB B-mode polarization</a> and <a href="/wiki/Inflation_(cosmology)" title="Inflation (cosmology)">cosmic inflation</a> based at <a href="/wiki/Lagrangian_point" title="Lagrangian point">L2</a></li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trojan_asteroid_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Trojan asteroid exploration (page does not exist)">Solar Power Sail</a>, a mission to <a href="/wiki/Jupiter" title="Jupiter">Jupiter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jupiter_trojans" class="mw-redirect" title="Jupiter trojans">Trojan asteroids</a> utilizing "hybrid propulsion" of <a href="/wiki/Solar_sail" title="Solar sail">solar sail</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ion_engine" class="mw-redirect" title="Ion engine">ion engines</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/SPICA_telescope" class="mw-redirect" title="SPICA telescope">SPICA</a>, a 2.5 meter infrared telescope to be placed at <a href="/wiki/Lagrangian_point" title="Lagrangian point">L2</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/DESTINY_PLUS" class="mw-redirect" title="DESTINY PLUS">DESTINY<sup>+</sup></a>, small scale technology demonstrator which will also conduct scientific observation of asteroid <a href="/wiki/3200_Phaethon" title="3200 Phaethon">3200 Phaethon</a></li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Focusing_Relativistic_Universe_and_Cosmic_Evolution&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Focusing Relativistic Universe and Cosmic Evolution (page does not exist)">FORCE</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> small scale hard x-ray observation with high sensitivity</li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Diffuse_Intergalactic_Oxygen_Surveyor&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Diffuse Intergalactic Oxygen Surveyor (page does not exist)">DIOS</a>, small scale x-ray observation mission to survey <a href="/wiki/Warm%E2%80%93hot_intergalactic_medium" title="Warm\xe2\x80\x93hot intergalactic medium">warm\xe2\x80\x93hot intergalactic medium</a></li>\n<li>APPROACH, small scale lunar penetrator mission</li>\n<li>HiZ-GUNDAM, small scale <a href="/wiki/Gamma_ray_burst" class="mw-redirect" title="Gamma ray burst">gamma ray burst</a> observation mission</li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solar-C&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Solar-C (page does not exist)">Solar-C</a>, solar observation</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/DECIGO" class="mw-redirect" title="DECIGO">Pre-DECIGO</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gravitational-wave_observatory" title="Gravitational-wave observatory">gravity wave observation</a> test mission</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/SELENE-2" title="SELENE-2">SELENE-2</a>, a moon landing mission</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hayabusa_Mk2/Marco_Polo" class="mw-redirect" title="Hayabusa Mk2/Marco Polo">Hayabusa Mk2/Marco Polo</a></li>\n<li>Space Solar Power System (SSPS), <a href="/wiki/Space-based_solar_power" title="Space-based solar power">space-based solar power</a> prototype launch in 2020, aiming for a full power system in 2030<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_space_program">Human space program</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=JAXA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Human space program">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sts-47-patch.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Sts-47-patch.png/220px-Sts-47-patch.png" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Sts-47-patch.png/330px-Sts-47-patch.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Sts-47-patch.png/440px-Sts-47-patch.png 2x" data-file-width="1021" data-file-height="656" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sts-47-patch.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <i>Spacelab-J</i> shuttle flight, funded by Japan, included several tons of Japanese science research equipment</div></div></div>\n<p>Japan has ten astronauts but has not yet developed its own manned spacecraft and is not currently developing one officially. A potentially manned <a href="/wiki/Space_shuttle" class="mw-redirect" title="Space shuttle">space shuttle</a>-<a href="/wiki/Spaceplane" title="Spaceplane">spaceplane</a> <a href="/wiki/HOPE-X" title="HOPE-X">HOPE-X</a> project launched by the conventional space launcher <a href="/wiki/H-II" title="H-II">H-II</a> was developed for several years (including test flights of <a href="/wiki/Hyflex" title="Hyflex">Hyflex</a>/<a href="/wiki/OREX" title="OREX">OREX</a> prototypes) but was postponed. The simpler manned capsule <a href="/wiki/Fuji_(Spacecraft)" class="mw-redirect" title="Fuji (Spacecraft)">Fuji</a> was proposed but not adopted. Projects for <a href="/wiki/Single_stage_to_orbit" class="mw-redirect" title="Single stage to orbit">single-stage to orbit</a>, horizontal takeoff <a href="/wiki/Reusable_launch_vehicle" class="mw-redirect" title="Reusable launch vehicle">reusable launch vehicle</a> and landing ASSTS and the <a href="/wiki/VTOL" title="VTOL">vertical takeoff and landing</a> <a href="/wiki/Kankoh-maru" title="Kankoh-maru">Kankoh-maru</a> also exist but have not been adopted.\n</p><p>The first Japanese citizen to fly in space was <a href="/wiki/Toyohiro_Akiyama" title="Toyohiro Akiyama">Toyohiro Akiyama</a>, a journalist sponsored by <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Broadcasting_System" title="Tokyo Broadcasting System">TBS</a>, who flew on the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_TM-11" title="Soyuz TM-11">Soyuz TM-11</a> in December 1990. He spent more than seven days in space on the <a href="/wiki/Mir" title="Mir">Mir</a> space station, in what the Soviets called their first commercial spaceflight which allowed them to earn $14 million.\n</p><p>Japan participates in US and international manned space programs including flights of Japanese astronauts on Russian <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_(spacecraft)" title="Soyuz (spacecraft)">Soyuz</a> spacecraft to the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">ISS</a>. One Space Shuttle mission (<a href="/wiki/STS-47" title="STS-47">STS-47</a>) in September 1992 was partially funded by Japan. This flight included JAXA\'s first astronaut in space, <a href="/wiki/Mamoru_Mohri" title="Mamoru Mohri">Mamoru Mohri</a>, as the Payload Specialist for the Spacelab-J, one of the European built <a href="/wiki/Spacelab" title="Spacelab">Spacelab</a> modules. This mission was also designated <i>Japan</i>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kibo_completed_view1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Kibo_completed_view1.jpg/220px-Kibo_completed_view1.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Kibo_completed_view1.jpg/330px-Kibo_completed_view1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Kibo_completed_view1.jpg/440px-Kibo_completed_view1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kibo_completed_view1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A view of the completed Kibo module.</div></div></div>\n<p>Three other NASA Space Shuttle missions (<a href="/wiki/STS-123" title="STS-123">STS-123</a>, <a href="/wiki/STS-124" title="STS-124">STS-124</a>, <a href="/wiki/STS-127" title="STS-127">STS-127</a>) in 2008\xe2\x80\x932009 delivered parts of the Japanese built spacelab-module <a href="/wiki/Kibo_(ISS_module)" title="Kibo (ISS module)">Kibo</a> to ISS.\n</p><p>Japanese plans for a manned lunar landing were in development but were shelved in early 2010 due to budget constraints.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In June 2014 Japan\'s science and technology ministry said it was considering a space mission to <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">Mars</a>. In a ministry paper it  indicated unmanned exploration, manned missions to Mars and long-term settlement on the <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">Moon</a> were objectives, for which international cooperation and support was going to be sought.<sup id="cite_ref-JapanMars_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JapanMars-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On October 18th, 2017, Japanese discovery of a "tunnel" under the surface of the moon has led to press-release.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> The tunnel seems to be suitable as a location for a base-of-operations of peaceful manned space missions, according to JAXA.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Supersonic_aircraft_development">Supersonic aircraft development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=JAXA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Supersonic aircraft development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Besides the H-IIA/B and <a href="/wiki/Epsilon_rocket" class="mw-redirect" title="Epsilon rocket">Epsilon</a> rockets, JAXA is also developing technology for a next-generation <a href="/wiki/Supersonic_transport" title="Supersonic transport">supersonic transport</a> that could become the commercial replacement for the <a href="/wiki/Concorde" title="Concorde">Concorde</a>. The design goal of the project (working name <a href="/wiki/Next_Generation_Supersonic_Transport" title="Next Generation Supersonic Transport">Next Generation Supersonic Transport</a>) is to develop a jet that can carry 300 passengers at <a href="/wiki/Mach_number" title="Mach number">Mach</a> 2. A subscale model of the jet underwent aerodynamic testing in September and October 2005 in Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>In 2015 JAXA performed tests aimed at reducing the effects of super sonic flight under the D-SEND program.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> The economic success of such a project is still unclear, and as a consequence the project has been met with limited interest from Japanese aerospace companies like Mitsubishi Heavy Industries so far.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reusable_launch_vehicles">Reusable launch vehicles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=JAXA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Reusable launch vehicles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Until 2003,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> JAXA (<a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Space_and_Astronautical_Science" title="Institute of Space and Astronautical Science">ISAS</a>) conducted research on a reusable launch vehicle under the <a href="/wiki/Reusable_Vehicle_Testing" title="Reusable Vehicle Testing">Reusable Vehicle Testing (RVT)</a> project.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_space_agencies_in_Japan">Other space agencies in Japan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=JAXA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Other space agencies in Japan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Not included into the JAXA organization is the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Space_Systems" title="Japan Space Systems">Japan Space Systems</a> (J-spacesystems), Japan\'s other space agency.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=JAXA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit
